<div id="review_967742690" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/967742690" />
    <a title="Will M." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20408288-will-m"><img alt="Will M." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452951660p2/20408288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/967742690?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will M." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will M." href="/user/show/20408288-will-m">Will M.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780385374927" href="/book/show/20360665-the-eye-of-minds">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=ya-sci-fi-dystopia">ya-sci-fi-dystopia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer967742690" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14561952874625049651"><br/>Kindly skip the sentences that were <u> underlined </u> as they will contain spoilers.<br/><br/><br/>Before I get into the review of the novel, I'd like to point out that I was expecting this to be a bad rip off of Ready Player One. RPO's one of my favorite novels, so I had mountain high expectations for The Eye of Minds. <br/><br/>Just like James Dashner's The Maze Runner, this one literally started with a mystery. I kinda like that about Dashner. A mystery at the very beginning tends to make the reader speculate possible eve</span>
  <span id="freeText14561952874625049651" style="display:none"><br />Kindly skip the sentences that were <u> underlined </u> as they will contain spoilers.<br /><br /><br />Before I get into the review of the novel, I'd like to point out that I was expecting this to be a bad rip off of Ready Player One. RPO's one of my favorite novels, so I had mountain high expectations for The Eye of Minds. <br /><br />Just like James Dashner's The Maze Runner, this one literally started with a mystery. I kinda like that about Dashner. A mystery at the very beginning tends to make the reader speculate possible events, although with that style, consistency is a must. <br /><br />Honestly there were a lot of problems with this novel. Some that cannot be overlooked. <br /><br />Michael, Sarah, and Bryson are best friends, but only in the VirtNet, not in the real world. That's not the problem though, the problem was that they were described as the smart ones. Sure, conceitedness is very evident in most novels, but like I said, consistency is necessary. They were introduced as smart kids, so I was expecting them to actually be smart. <u> But blindly accepting VNS' mission/forced task was clearly <b> stupid </b>. Yes, I know they threatened Michael, and also cut him off VirtNet, and that triggered his choice to accept the mission, but, if he's really smart, he could've found a way out of the threat. But instead, he dumbly followed VNS. Thus causing havoc in his life. </u><br /><br />Another terrible thing I noticed was that Dashner didn't explain a very important concept well, and that's tangent. I understood tangent as something from my Trigonometry class, those who aren't computer nerds would be unsure of the meaning. I did use my context clues skills and decided to conclude that the meaning of tangent here was something that exists because it was made, and something in a computer. I wanted to be certain though, so I decided to check it out on the net. Here's what I got from Urban Dictionary:<br /><br /><i> Mathematician who got back from the beach. <br /><br />Noun: A completely and utterly worthless computer company that sells blocks a shit, aka laptops, to college students.<br /><br />one that is<br />a. radio disc jockey that touches a circle of toenails at one toenail<br />b. a polar bear<br />c. an idiot of the 270th degree; three pie halves in radians </i><br /><br />My point being, the author should've <i> clearly </i> described what the hell tangent meant. I'm sure that some people would say "use your common sense, it's so obvious that it's all about computer shit", well, that's your opinion of it. I did speculate about it having to do with computers, so I guess I used my common sense. <br /><br />Now, to talk about things that I liked about this, as to support my 4 stars.<br /><br />Kaine. He was very likeable, especially this being a YA novel. Most antagonists in YA tend to become boring and weak. Kaine on the other hand, proved to be the monstrous devil he clearly was. In fact, I liked him more than all of the protagonists combined. That's not necessarily bad in a novel, one liking the antagonist more, but clearly the author intended Michael and his friends to be superior. <br /><br /><u> The huge plot twist in the end, and the one near the end were very good. I did not see them coming, that being said, the rating from 3 moved up to 4. Without those plot twist of Kaine being a tangent, then Michael being a tangent, this would be one hell of a mediocre novel. </u><br /><br />One more thing that I liked would be, believe it or not, the somewhat non-existence of romance in this novel. That was a huge thing for me, as I was expecting little romance, if not none because of the blurb. Most, if not all, YA novels revolve around romance, and most of the time, it should be called forced romance. I guess <b> most </b> YA authors write for the ladies, and that's why I really filter out YA novels, and only read the ones that were meant for both genders. This novel was <b> not </b> chick-lit, not even a little. It was also <b> not </b> romance-YA-lit. That being said, this actually turned out to be a good novel for me, in terms of that standard. The only hint of romance would be of <u> Michael and Sarah in the end, where they promised each other stuff. But that could also be interpreted as a best friend gesture, idk, it depends on the reader I guess. </u><br /><br />Another thing I'd like to point out before ending this review would be the ignorance of people when it comes to the blurb/synopsis of the novel, or even the genre at all. Kindly read it first, and decide if you really want to read the novel. Don't just read something because of the hype it's been receiving, because if the blurb bored the hell out of you, what more would the novel. I'll be honest and say that I tend to read novels without really reading the blurb, and end up hating the novel. Although if a person didn't like the blurb, but ended up loving the novel, then that makes the author a really good writer. A very difficult thing to achieve, so I'd suggest the reading of the blurb properly part. <br /><br />The huge plot twist would result into an obvious sequel, and I heard that this was going to be a trilogy, and I can't wait to read the next book. This had an original plot, and I guess I really liked this one. I didn't mind the "writing style" of Dashner, that everyone seemed to hate. It was bearable, for me at least. A solid 4 stars, and I'd like to point out that this may bring back hope to the YA genre(alongside Steelheart- Brandon Sanderson), for me at least. If you're a Sci-Fi fan, I'd give this one a try. It was a good short read, not disappointing, but also not amazing. Kindly remind yourself that this is a YA novel, so don't expect much. Bad world building, and mediocre character development. In terms of YA though, this could be considered amazing, especially when compared to others of the same genre. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14561952874625049651" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1156809374" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10182135564070384583">The Eye of Minds by James Dashner is the first book in the Mortality Doctrine series. After reading the Maze Runner (also by James Dashner) I thought he was a great author and I thought I'd give this book a try. It was just as great and original if not better. This book is about a boy named Michael in the future world. He is a great user of VirtNet, a whole new virtual world where your coffin allows you to feel everything like it 's the reality. Michel and his friends Sara and Bryson are great p</span>
  <span id="freeText10182135564070384583" style="display:none">The Eye of Minds by James Dashner is the first book in the Mortality Doctrine series. After reading the Maze Runner (also by James Dashner) I thought he was a great author and I thought I'd give this book a try. It was just as great and original if not better. This book is about a boy named Michael in the future world. He is a great user of VirtNet, a whole new virtual world where your coffin allows you to feel everything like it 's the reality. Michel and his friends Sara and Bryson are great players with hacking and coding skills that are beyond many people's abilities. One gamer, Kaine has been causing mayhem among the virtual world. He's a hacker that can do more to VirtNet then they ever imagined. When they turn to Michael and his friends for help, the future of VirtNet is in his hands and danger in the virtual world is real. Will they be able to defeat Kaine? Well, you'll have to read to find out!!!<br /><br />I'd recommend this book to anyone who wants a break from the typical air in stories we've seen lately. (The Hunger Games, Divergent, etc.) This book is really unique and Dashner's ideas are very unique. It's creative and it was nice to read something different for a change.<br /><br />James Dashner was already very successful with his well known book, "The Maze Runner." The Eye of Minds was also praised by many reviewers including the NY Times coauthor. <br /><br />This book deserves to be recognized. I'd also recommend this book to those who liked The Maze Runner. It's just as good as Dashner's bestseller.<br /></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2953149920" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2953149920" />
    <a title="⭐Anni⭐ (Book Princess)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63666087-anni-book-princess"><img alt="⭐Anni⭐ (Book Princess)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592328395p2/63666087.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2953149920?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="⭐Anni⭐ (Book Princess)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="⭐Anni⭐ (Book Princess)" href="/user/show/63666087-anni-book-princess">⭐Anni⭐ (Book Princess)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63666087-anni-book-princess?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63666087-anni-book-princess?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2953149920" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1585914231424788607">This wasn't bad, but it wasn't especially good either. The Eye of Minds was a very quick read though, and I can see teens, especially boys, liking the book.<br/><br/><b>What I liked:</b><br/>- the action and fast pacing. There was a lot of action that kept the story going.<br/>- the easy writing style. It made for a really quick read.<br/>- the overall idea. It wasn't anything new (consider Ready Player One), but I still think virtual reality is am exciting topic to explore.<br/>- the final plot twist, I didn't see that coming!<br/><br/><b>What</b></span>
  <span id="freeText1585914231424788607" style="display:none">This wasn't bad, but it wasn't especially good either. The Eye of Minds was a very quick read though, and I can see teens, especially boys, liking the book.<br /><br /><b>What I liked:</b><br />- the action and fast pacing. There was a lot of action that kept the story going.<br />- the easy writing style. It made for a really quick read.<br />- the overall idea. It wasn't anything new (consider Ready Player One), but I still think virtual reality is am exciting topic to explore.<br />- the final plot twist, I didn't see that coming!<br /><br /><b>What I didn't like:</b><br />- the characters. I didn't connect to any of them. Especially Michael, the MC, struck me as really naive. There wasn't much character development either.<br />- not enough world building (both in game and in reality). Some interesting concepts were there, but they weren't explored enough.<br />- some scenes were unnecessary brutal, especially for a ya book. There's a reason certain pc games are for certain age groups only.<br /><br /><b>In conclusion</b>, The Eye of Minds kept me entertained for a couple of hours. The idea was good and well executed, but there wasn't nearly enough character development. I'd recommend the books for teenagers who like gaming and the concept of virtual reality, I myself won't continue with this trilogy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1585914231424788607" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2837818440" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4369813406970041344">I didn't really enjoy reading this book. It was very boring, and predictable. You could tell what would happen a lot of times in the book. The beginning was kind of hard to get into and understand, but then it became easy to understand. At the end of the book when they were fighting Kaine it became a little bit more interesting. The only thing that I didn't know would happen was parts at the end, like Sarah dying in lava, and Michael being a tangent. Then after finding out he was a tangent findi</span>
  <span id="freeText4369813406970041344" style="display:none">I didn't really enjoy reading this book. It was very boring, and predictable. You could tell what would happen a lot of times in the book. The beginning was kind of hard to get into and understand, but then it became easy to understand. At the end of the book when they were fighting Kaine it became a little bit more interesting. The only thing that I didn't know would happen was parts at the end, like Sarah dying in lava, and Michael being a tangent. Then after finding out he was a tangent finding out that Kaine sent him to be a real human, and try to get him to take over the VirtNet world. </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('STkf0BrvUk/+WWSpAFCZw8FCeFMAAtgT/gza67bApmczyTo2HvXQX0diuLYE2UAf4IhnNPTdzyaXzrKceZtbJA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('glnB2f2/ANkqHOu5k29fbjjwY/0rSDDaJY1Pt17Rv9P4qeQ/+aWCyZMnN6aX5oayGTp8mt+XJ+9MTyfAkYpCkA==')})
  }
//]]>
